<!--Polyfills CustomEvent constructor in IE. Allows us to use events to manage race conditions in client side js-->
<script>
    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

        window.CustomEvent = CustomEvent;
    })();
</script>

    <meta name="journal_id" content="41597"/>

    <meta name="dc.title" content="A chromosome-level genome assembly of the Chinese tupelo Nyssa sinensis"/>

    <meta name="dc.source" content="Scientific Data 2019 6:1"/>

    <meta name="dc.format" content="text/html"/>

    <meta name="dc.publisher" content="Nature Publishing Group"/>

    <meta name="dc.date" content="2019-11-25"/>

    <meta name="dc.type" content="OriginalPaper"/>

    <meta name="dc.language" content="En"/>

    <meta name="dc.copyright" content="2019 The Author(s)"/>

    <meta name="dc.rightsAgent" content="journalpermissions@springernature.com"/>

    <meta name="dc.description" content="The deciduous Chinese tupelo (Nyssa sinensis&#160;Oliv.) is a popular ornamental tree for the spectacular autumn leaf color. Here, using single-molecule sequencing and chromosome conformation capture data, we report a high-quality, chromosome-level genome assembly of N. sinensis. PacBio long reads were de novo assembled into 647 polished contigs with a total length of 1,001.42 megabases (Mb) and an N50 size of 3.62&#8201;Mb, which is in line with genome sizes estimated using flow cytometry and the k-mer analysis. These contigs were further clustered and ordered into 22 pseudo-chromosomes based on Hi-C data, matching the chromosome counts in Nyssa obtained from previous cytological studies. In addition, a total of 664.91&#8201;Mb of repetitive elements were identified and a total of 37,884 protein-coding genes were predicted in the genome of N. sinensis. All data were deposited in publicly available repositories, and should be a valuable resource for genomics, evolution, and conservation biology. 
                
                  
                    
                    
                    
                  
                
               Machine-accessible metadata file describing the reported data: https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.10069796"/>

            <div class="c-article-body">
                <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>The deciduous Chinese tupelo (<i>Nyssa sinensis</i>Â Oliv.) is a popular ornamental tree for the spectacular autumn leaf color. Here, using single-molecule sequencing and chromosome conformation capture data, we report a high-quality, chromosome-level genome assembly of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>. PacBio long reads were <i>de novo</i> assembled into 647 polished contigs with a total length of 1,001.42 megabases (Mb) and an N50 size of 3.62âMb, which is in line with genome sizes estimated using flow cytometry and the <i>k</i>-mer analysis. These contigs were further clustered and ordered into 22 pseudo-chromosomes based on Hi-C data, matching the chromosome counts in <i>Nyssa</i> obtained from previous cytological studies. In addition, a total of 664.91âMb of repetitive elements were identified and a total of 37,884 protein-coding genes were predicted in the genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>. All data were deposited in publicly available repositories, and should be a valuable resource for genomics, evolution, and conservation biology.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Abs2" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs2-section"><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs2-content">
                <div class="c-article-table-container"><div class="c-article-table-border c-table-scroll-wrapper"><div class="c-table-scroll-wrapper__content" data-component-scroll-wrapper=""><table class="data last-table"><tbody><tr><td class="u-text-left ">
                          Measurement(s)
                        </td><td class="u-text-left ">
                          whole genome sequencing assay â¢ transcription profiling assay â¢ sequence_assembly â¢ sequence annotation
                        </td></tr><tr><td class="u-text-left ">
                          Technology Type(s)
                        </td><td class="u-text-left ">
                          DNA sequencing â¢ RNA sequencing assay â¢ genome assembly â¢ bioinformatics analysis
                        </td></tr><tr><td class="u-text-left ">
                          Sample Characteristic - Organism
                        </td><td class="u-text-left ">
                          Nyssa sinensis
                        </td></tr><tr><td class="u-text-left ">
                          Sample Characteristic - Environment
                        </td><td class="u-text-left ">
                          terrestrial biome
                        </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>
              <p>Machine-accessible metadata file describing the reported data: <a href="https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.10069796">https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.10069796</a></p></div></div></section>

                    <section aria-labelledby="Sec1" data-title="Background &amp; Summary"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Background &amp; Summary</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p><i>Nyssa sinensis</i>Â Oliv., commonly known as Chinese tupelo, is a deciduous tree with ovate leaves, which turn brilliant red, orange, and yellow in autumn. It belongs to the family Nyssaceae within the order Cornales, and is native to southern China and Vietnam. The genus <i>Nyssa</i> comprises three species in North America (i.e., <i>N</i>. <i>aquatica</i>, <i>N</i>. <i>ogeche</i>, and <i>N</i>. <i>sylvatica</i>), three in eastern Asia (i.e., <i>N</i>. <i>javanica</i>, <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>, and <i>N</i>. <i>yunnanensis</i>), and one in Costa Rica (i.e., <i>N</i>. <i>talamancana</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Wen, J. &amp; Stuessy, T. F. The phylogeny and biogeography of Nyssa (Cornaceae). Syst. Bot. 18, 68â79 (1993)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d24693e613">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Wang, N. et al. Phylogeny and a revised classification of the Chinese species of Nyssa (Nyssaceae) based on morphological and molecular data. Taxon 61, 344â354 (2012)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d24693e616">2</a></sup>. Thus, it is one of the plant genera that exhibit a classical disjunct distribution between eastern Asia and North America. In addition, the fossil record of <i>Nyssa</i> is very rich<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Wen, J. &amp; Stuessy, T. F. The phylogeny and biogeography of Nyssa (Cornaceae). Syst. Bot. 18, 68â79 (1993)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d24693e624">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Eyde, R. H. Fossil record and ecology of Nyssa (Cornaceae). Bot. Rev. 63, 97â123 (1997)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d24693e627">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Manchester, S. R., GrÃ­msson, F. &amp; Zetter, R. Assessing the fossil record of asterids in the context of our current phylogenetic framework. Ann. Missouri Bot. Gard. 100, 329â363 (2015)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d24693e630">4</a></sup>, making it ideal for studying the evolutionary history of Tertiary relict floras.</p><p>The genome of <i>Camptotheca acuminata</i> (Nyssaceae) has recently been sequenced using the Illumina platform<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Zhao, D. et al. De novo genome assembly of Camptotheca acuminata, a natural source of the anti-cancer compound camptothecin. GigaScience 6, gix065 (2017)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d24693e640">5</a></sup>, and the final assembly is 403.17 megabases (Mb) with a contig N50 size of 107.59 kilobases (kb). So far, this is the only sequenced genome within the order Cornales. Here, we utilized a combination of the PacBio long-read sequencing technology<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Eid, J. et al. Real-time DNA sequencing from single polymerase molecules. Science 323, 133â138 (2009)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d24693e644">6</a></sup> and the high-throughput chromosome conformation capture (Hi-C) technique<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="van Berkum, N. L. et al. Hi-C: a method to study the three-dimensional architecture of genomes. J. Vis. Exp. 39, e1869 (2010)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d24693e648">7</a></sup> to generate the genome sequence of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>. Long reads were <i>de novo</i> assembled into 647 polished contigs with a total length of 1,001.42âMb and an N50 size of 3.62âMb, which is in line with genome sizes estimated using flow cytometry and the <i>k</i>-mer analysis. These contigs were further clustered and ordered into 22 pseudo-chromosomes based on Hi-C data. Our results provide the first high-quality, chromosome-level genome assembly for the order Cornales, which should be a valuable resource for genomics, evolution, and conservation biology.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec2" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">Sample collection and high-throughput sequencing</h3><p>We sampled a single individual of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> from the Kunming Botanical Garden, Yunnan, China. The total genomic DNA was extracted from fresh leaves using a modified CTAB method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Doyle, J. J. &amp; Doyle, J. L. A rapid DNA isolation procedure for small quantities of fresh leaf tissue. Phytochem. Bull. 19, 11â15 (1987)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d24693e683">8</a></sup>, and sequenced using the PacBio Sequel System (for genome assembly) and the Illumina HiSeq. 4000 System (for genome survey and base level correction after the assembly). Here, one library with an insertion size of 350âbp was prepared for the Illumina platform and 20-kb libraries were constructed for the PacBio platform according to the manufacturersâ protocols. A total of 104.34 gigabases (Gb) of polymerase reads were generated using the PacBio platform, and a total of 104.19âGb (coverage of 99.12Ã) of subreads were obtained after removing adaptors in polymerase reads (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab1">1</a>). The N50 read length reached 22.26âkb and 14.53âkb for polymerase reads and subreads, respectively. A total of 58.92âGb of 150-bp paired-end reads were generated using the Illumina platform, and a total of 58.83âGb (coverage of 55.97Ã) of reads were obtained after adapter trimming and quality filtering (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab1">1</a>). In addition, the Hi-C library was constructed using young leaf tissue from the same individual of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>, and sequenced using the Illumina platform. A total of 126.81âGb (coverage of 120.63Ã) of 150-bp paired-end reads were obtained after adapter trimming and quality filtering (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab1">1</a>), which were later applied to extend the contiguity of the genome assembly to the chromosomal level. Furthermore, leaves and flowers were collected from the same individual of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>, and RNA-Seq reads were generated for genome annotation using the Illumina platform. A total of 17.36âGb of 150-bp paired-end reads were obtained after adapter trimming and quality filtering (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab1">1</a>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-2"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table 1 Summary of sequencing data generated in this study.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/tables/2"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Genome size and heterozygosity estimation</h3><p>The genome size of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> was first estimated using the <i>k</i>-mer analysis with Jellyfish<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="MarÃ§ais, G. &amp; Kingsford, C. A fast, lock-free approach for efficient parallel counting of occurrences of k-mers. Bioinformatics 27, 764â770 (2011)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d24693e820">9</a></sup>. The 17-mer frequency of Illumina short reads followed a Poisson distribution, with the highest peak occurring at a depth of 45 (Fig.Â <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Fig1">1</a>). The estimated genome size was 1,051.16âMb, and the heterozygosity rate of the genome was 0.87% (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab2">2</a>). In addition, we performed flow cytometry analysis using <i>Vigna radiata</i> as the internal standard, and the genome size of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> was estimated at 992âMb.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Fig. 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41597-019-0296-y/MediaObjects/41597_2019_296_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-1-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41597-019-0296-y/MediaObjects/41597_2019_296_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="582" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p>The <i>k</i>-mer analysis (<i>k</i>â=â17) for estimating the genome size of <i>Nyssa sinensis</i>. The x-axis refers to the <i>k</i>-mer depth; the y-axis refers to the frequency of the <i>k</i>-mer for a given depth.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-3"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab2" data-test="table-caption">Table 2 Summary of the <i>k</i>-mer analysis for estimating the genome size of <i>Nyssa sinensis</i>. 150-bp paired-end reads were generated using the Illumina platform, and a total of 58.83âGb of reads were obtained after adapter trimming and quality filtering. The frequency of each <i>k</i>-mer was calculated and plotted in Fig.Â <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Fig1">1</a>.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/tables/3"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5"><i>De novo</i> genome assembly and pseudo-chromosome construction</h3><p>After the self-error correction step, the PacBio long reads were assembled into contigs using the hierarchical genome assembly process (HGAP)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Chin, C.-S. et al. Nonhybrid, finished microbial genome assemblies from long-read SMRT sequencing data. Nat. Methods 10, 563â569 (2013)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d24693e936">10</a></sup> as implemented in the FALCON assembler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Pendleton, M. et al. Assembly and diploid architecture of an individual human genome via single-molecule technologies. Nat. Methods 12, 780â786 (2015)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d24693e940">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Chin, C.-S. et al. Phased diploid genome assembly with single-molecule real-time sequencing. Nat. Methods 13, 1050â1054 (2016)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d24693e943">12</a></sup>. In addition, two rounds of polishing were applied to the assembled contigs using the Quiver algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Chin, C.-S. et al. Nonhybrid, finished microbial genome assemblies from long-read SMRT sequencing data. Nat. Methods 10, 563â569 (2013)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d24693e947">10</a></sup> with the PacBio long reads, and another round of the genome-wide base-level correction was performed using Pilon<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Walker, B. J. et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. Plos One 9, e112963 (2014)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d24693e951">13</a></sup> with the Illumina short reads. Finally, the Purge Haplotigs pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Roach, M. J., Schmidt, S. A. &amp; Borneman, A. R. Purge Haplotigs: allelic contig reassignment for third-gen diploid genome assemblies. BMC Bioinformatics 19, 460 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d24693e955">14</a></sup> was run to produce an improved, deduplicated assembly. The resulting genome assembly of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> contained 1,001.42âMb of sequences in 647 polished contigs with an N50 size of 3.62âMb (contigs shorter than 100âbp were discarded; TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab3">3</a>), and the overall GC-content was 35.98%.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-4"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab3" data-test="table-caption">Table 3 Summary of genome assemblies of <i>Nyssa sinensis</i> created at different stages of the assembly process.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/tables/4"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Construction of pseudo-chromosomes followed the previous study<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Yin, D. et al. Genome of an allotetraploid wild peanut Arachis monticola: a de novo assembly. GigaScience 7, giy066 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1054">15</a></sup> using the Hi-C library. Briefly, the clean Hi-C reads were mapped to the assembled contigs using the BurrowsâWheeler Aligner<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with BurrowsâWheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754â1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1058">16</a></sup> (BWA), and only uniquely mapped read pairs were considered for downstream analysis. Duplicate removal, sorting, and quality assessment were performed using HiC-Pro<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Servant, N. et al. HiC-Pro: an optimized and flexible pipeline for Hi-C data processing. Genome Biol. 16, 259 (2015)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1062">17</a></sup>. The assembled contigs were then clustered, ordered, and oriented into pseudo-chromosomes using LACHESIS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Burton, J. N. et al. Chromosome-scale scaffolding of de novo genome assemblies based on chromatin interactions. Nat. Biotechnol. 31, 1119â1125 (2013)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1066">18</a></sup>. A total of 585 contigs spanning 1,000.96âMb (i.e., 99.95% of the assembly) were clustered into 22 chromosome groups (Fig.Â <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Fig2">2</a>), matching the chromosome counts in <i>Nyssa</i> (<i>n</i>â=â22) based on cytological studies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dermen, H. Cytological studies of Cornus. J. Arnold Arbor. 13, 410â416 (1932)." href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1080">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mehra, P. N. &amp; Bawa, K. S. Chromosomal evolution in tropical hardwoods. Evolution 23, 466â481 (1969)." href="#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1080_1">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Goldblatt, P. A contribution to cytology in Cornales. Ann. Missouri Bot. Gard. 65, 650â655 (1978)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1083">21</a></sup>. In addition, of the clustered contigs, 382 contigs spanning 968.49âMb (i.e., 96.71% of the assembly) were successfully ordered and orientated (Online-only TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab7">1</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Fig. 2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41597-019-0296-y/MediaObjects/41597_2019_296_Fig2_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-2-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41597-019-0296-y/MediaObjects/41597_2019_296_Fig2_HTML.png" alt="figure2" loading="lazy" width="685" height="684" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p>Interaction heat map of Hi-C links among chromosome groups for <i>Nyssa sinensis</i>. The assembled genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> was divided into 100-kb non-overlapping windows (or bins), and valid interaction links of Hi-C data were calculated between each pair of bins. The binary logarithm of each link number is coded using colors ranging from light yellow to dark red, indicating the frequency of Hi-C interaction links from low to high. LG0âLG21 represent the 22 chromosome groups inferred by LACHESIS.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">The annotation of repetitive elements</h3><p>To annotate repetitive elements in the genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>, we utilized a combination of evidence-based and <i>de novo</i> approaches. The genome assembly was first searched using RepeatMasker (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org">http://www.repeatmasker.org</a>) against the Repbase database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Bao, W., Kojima, K. K. &amp; Kohany, O. Repbase Update, a database of repetitive elements in eukaryotic genomes. Mobile DNA 6, 11 (2015)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1128">22</a></sup>. Next, a <i>de novo</i> repetitive element library was constructed using RepeatModeler (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatModeler/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatModeler/</a>), which employed results from RECON<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Bao, Z. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Automated de novo identification of repeat sequence families in sequenced genomes. Genome Res. 12, 1269â1276 (2002)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1140">23</a></sup> and RepeatScout<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Price, A. L., Jones, N. C. &amp; Pevzner, P. A. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21, i351âi358 (2005)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1144">24</a></sup>. This <i>de novo</i> repetitive element library was then utilized by RepeatMasker to annotate repetitive elements. Results from these two runs of RepeatMasker were merged together. A total of 664.91âMb of repetitive elements (i.e., 66.40% of the assembly) were identified in the genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab4">4</a>), including retroelements (32.51%), DNA transposons (11.23%), tandem repeats (2.95%), and unclassified elements (19.71%). Thus, the percentage of predicted repetitive elements in the genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> is much higher in comparison with that in the closely related species <i>C</i>. <i>acuminata</i> (i.e., 35.6%<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Zhao, D. et al. De novo genome assembly of Camptotheca acuminata, a natural source of the anti-cancer compound camptothecin. GigaScience 6, gix065 (2017)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1174">5</a></sup>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-5"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab4" data-test="table-caption">Table 4 Summary of repetitive elements annotated in the genome of <i>Nyssa sinensis</i>.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/tables/5"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Long terminal repeat (LTR) retrotransposons are prevalent in plant genomes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Ou, S. &amp; Jiang, N. LTR_retriever: a highly accurate and sensitive program for identification of long terminal repeat retrotransposons. Plant Physiol. 176, 1410â1422 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1278">25</a></sup>. In order to develop high-quality gene annotation, we additionally identified LTR retrotransposons in the genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> using a combination of four programs (i.e., LTR_FINDER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W265âW268 (2007)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1288">26</a></sup>, LTRharvest<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Ellinghaus, D., Kurtz, S. &amp; Willhoeft, U. LTRharvest, an efficient and flexible software for de novo detection of LTR retrotransposons. BMC Bioinformatics 9, 18 (2008)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1292">27</a></sup>, LTR_retriever<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Ou, S. &amp; Jiang, N. LTR_retriever: a highly accurate and sensitive program for identification of long terminal repeat retrotransposons. Plant Physiol. 176, 1410â1422 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1297">25</a></sup>, and RepeatMasker). Here, LTR_FINDER and LTRharvest were used for initial identification of LTR retrotransposons; LTR_retriever was then used to filter out false positives and estimate the insertion time for each intact LTR retrotransposon; finally, RepeatMasker was used for annotation of LTR retrotransposons. Our results suggested that when comparing with <i>C</i>. <i>acuminata</i>, LTR retrotransposons in the genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> had recently undergone a rapid proliferation, particularly the Ty3-<i>gypsy</i> family (Fig.Â <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Fig3">3</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Fig. 3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 3</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41597-019-0296-y/MediaObjects/41597_2019_296_Fig3_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-3-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41597-019-0296-y/MediaObjects/41597_2019_296_Fig3_HTML.png" alt="figure3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="658" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p>Estimated insertion time of full-length long terminal repeat (LTR) retrotransposons in the genomes of <i>Nyssa sinensis</i> and <i>Camptotheca acuminata</i>.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">Protein-coding gene prediction and functional annotation</h3><p>The identification of protein-coding genes in the assembled genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> was based on transcriptome data and <i>ab initio</i> prediction. First, two strategies (i.e., <i>de novo</i> and genome-guided assembly) were applied to assemble RNA-Seq reads into transcripts using Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644â652 (2011)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1355">28</a></sup>. In order to use Trinity in genome-guided mode, RNA-Seq reads were first aligned to the assembled genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> using HISAT2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Kim, D., Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. HISAT: a fast spliced aligner with low memory requirements. Nat. Methods 12, 357â360 (2015)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1366">29</a></sup>. These two transcriptome assemblies were then merged. To generate the initial gene models for training AUGUSTUS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Stanke, M. &amp; Morgenstern, B. AUGUSTUS: a web server for gene prediction in eukaryotes that allows user-defined constraints. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W465âW467 (2005)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1370">30</a></sup>, our assembled transcripts were processed and utilized to identify open reading frames (ORFs) by the Program to Assemble Spliced Alignments<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the Program to Assemble Spliced Alignments. Genome Biol. 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1374">31</a></sup> (PASA). AUGUSTUS was then utilized for <i>ab initio</i> gene prediction based on (i) a generalized hidden Markov model (HMM) and (ii) semi-Markov conditional random field (CRF). In addition, extrinsic evidence was incorporated into AUGUSTUS using a hints file, which was generated by aligning RNA-Seq reads to the hard-masked genome assembly with HISAT2. Lastly, untranslated regions (UTRs) and alternative splicing variations were annotated using PASA. A total of 37,884 protein-coding genes were predicted in the genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab5">5</a>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-6"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab5" data-test="table-caption">Table 5 Summary of protein-coding genes predicted in the genome of <i>Nyssa sinensis</i>.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/tables/6"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>For functional annotation, our predicted protein-coding genes were searched against the Swiss-Prot and TrEMBL databases<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Boeckmann, B. et al. The SWISS-PROT protein knowledgebase and its supplement TrEMBL in 2003. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 365â370 (2003)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1442">32</a></sup> using BLAST+<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1446">33</a></sup> with and <i>E</i>-value threshold of 1e-05, as well as the InterPro database using InterProScan 5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics 30, 1236â1240 (2014)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1453">34</a></sup>. In addition, for predicted protein-coding genes, gene ontology (GO) annotations were performed using Blast2GO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Conesa, A. et al. Blast2GO: a universal tool for annotation, visualization and analysis in functional genomics research. Bioinformatics 21, 3674â3676 (2005)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1457">35</a></sup>, and KEGG orthology (KO) identifiers were assigned using KEGG Automatic Annotation Server<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Moriya, Y., Itoh, M., Okuda, S., Yoshizawa, A. C. &amp; Kanehisa, M. KAAS: an automatic genome annotation and pathway reconstruction server. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W182âW185 (2007)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1462">36</a></sup> (KAAS). A total of 36,185 genes (i.e., 95.52% of all predicted protein-coding genes) were successfully annotated by at least one database (TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab6">6</a>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-7"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab6" data-test="table-caption">Table 6 Summary of functional annotation of protein-coding genes in the genome of <i>Nyssa sinensis</i>.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y/tables/7"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec8" data-title="Data Records"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec8-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec8">Data Records</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec8-content"><p>PacBio Sequel long reads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;http://identifiers.org/ncbi/insdc.sra:SRX6405746&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1549">37</a></sup>, Illumina paired-end reads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;http://identifiers.org/ncbi/insdc.sra:SRX6441717&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1553">38</a></sup>, Hi-C reads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;http://identifiers.org/ncbi/insdc.sra:SRX6441715&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1557">39</a></sup>, and RNA-Seq reads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;http://identifiers.org/ncbi/insdc.sra:SRX6441716&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1561">40</a></sup> have been deposited in NCBI Sequence Read Archive (SRA). The genome assembly and annotation of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> have been deposited in CoGe<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Yang, X. et al. A chromosome-level genome assembly of the Chinese tupelo Nyssa sinensis. CoGe, &#xA;https://genomevolution.org/CoGe/GenomeInfo.pl?gid=55419&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1572">41</a></sup>, Figshare<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Yang, X. et al. A chromosome-level genome assembly of the Chinese tupelo Nyssa sinensis. figshare, &#xA;https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.8872700&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1576">42</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Yang, X. et al. A chromosome-level genome assembly of the Chinese tupelo Nyssa sinensis. figshare, &#xA;https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.8872721&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1579">43</a></sup>, and GenBank<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Yang, X. et al. Nyssa sinensis isolate J267, whole genome shotgun sequencing project. GenBank, &#xA;http://identifiers.org/ncbi/insdc:VIRR00000000&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1583">44</a></sup>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec9" data-title="Technical Validation"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec9-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec9">Technical Validation</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec9-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Total RNA quality assessment</h3><p>The quality of total RNA was evaluated using (i) agarose gel electrophoresis for RNA degradation and potential contamination, (ii) NanoDrop spectrophotometer for preliminary quantitation, and (iii) Agilent 2100 Bioanalyzer for RNA integrity and quantitation. Total RNA samples included in this study had an RNA integrity number (RIN) of 9.7â10 and an rRNA ratio of 1.5, which were then enriched for mRNA via an oligo(dT)âmagnetic bead method.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Quality filtering of Illumina data</h3><p>Illumina raw data were first filtered using Trimmomatic<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Bolger, A. M., Lohse, M. &amp; Usadel, B. Trimmomatic: a flexible trimmer for Illumina sequence data. Bioinformatics 30, 2114â2120 (2014)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1607">45</a></sup> to remove paired-end reads if either of the reads contained (i) adapter sequences, (ii) more than 10% of N bases, and (iii) more than 20% of bases with a Phred quality score less than 5.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Assessing the completeness and accuracy of the genome assembly</h3><p>We first evaluated the completeness of the assembly using CEGMA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Parra, G., Bradnam, K. &amp; Korf, I. CEGMA: a pipeline to accurately annotate core genes in eukaryotic genomes. Bioinformatics 23, 1061â1067 (2007)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1619">46</a></sup> and BUSCO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="SimÃ£o, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210â3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1623">47</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Waterhouse, R. M. et al. BUSCO applications from quality assessments to gene prediction and phylogenomics. Mol. Biol. Evol. 35, 543â548 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1626">48</a></sup>. Out of the 248 core eukaryotic genes in CEGMA, 235 (94.8%) complete matches and 244 (98.4%) complete plus partial matches were found in the assembled genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i>. In addition, 93.4% complete and 2.2% partial of the 1,440 plant-specific BUSCO genes were identified in the assembly. Second, the accuracy of the assembly was assessed using our Illumina short reads. In total, 94.51% of the filtered short reads (58.83âGb, TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#Tab1">1</a>) were mapped to the assembled genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> using BWA, which covered 99.89% of the assembly. Furthermore, Single-nucleotide polymorphisms (SNPs) were called and filtered using SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Li, H. et al. The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41597-019-0296-y#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d24693e1646">49</a></sup>, and a total of 5,046,556 SNPs with a sequencing depth between 10Ã and 100Ã were identified, consisting of 5,040,788 heterozygous SNPs and 5,768 homozygous SNPs. The low rate of homozygous SNPs (0.0006% of the assembled genome) suggested the high accuracy of the assembly. Finally, the assembled genome of <i>N</i>. <i>sinensis</i> was divided into 10-kb non-overlapping windows, and the scatter plot of the sequencing depth versus the GC-content based on 10-kb windows indicated no contamination of foreign DNA in the assembly.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="code-availability" data-title="Code availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="code-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="code-availability">Code availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="code-availability-content">
              
              <p>Sequencing data were generated using the software provided by sequencer manufacturers, and processed following the instruction manual of the software cited above. No custom codes were generated for this work.</p>
